LP
(Adds quotes and background)

MADRID, July 12 (Reuters) - Spain's telecoms regulator, the CMT, is asking the government to appeal the 152 million euro ($209.5 million) fine imposed by the European Commission against Telefonica  , the regulator said on Thursday.

TD
The fine was imposed against the country's dominant operator because it was considered to be squeezing out high-speed internet rivals.

Telefonica  stock was up 1.5 percent at 1443 GMT, shortly after the CMT statement, outperforming
Spain's Ibex stock index <.IBEX> which was 0.68 percent higher.

The EU fine -- the highest ever awarded against a telephony company -- "seriously and profoundly" damaged the CMT's powers as a regulator and threatened the powers of all national regulators, the CMT said in a statement.

"Indirect wholesale access [to ADSL] is also a non-existent service in many Member States and the European Commission has never demanded its regulation considering that it does not determine the competitive development of markets", it said.

Spanish industry minister Joan Clos had already said the government was considering whether to appeal the fine which he called a "spectacular amount".
The fine is the second-highest the European Union's top  antitrust regulator has levied in an "abuse
of dominance" case, beaten by almost half a billion euros which Microsoft had to pay in 2004.

HD          EU: Confident Telefonica  Ruling Will Hold Up If Appealed
WC          251 words

SC           DJI
LA           English

BRUSSELS (Dow Jones)--The  European Commission Friday said it is confident its decision to fineTelefonica SA (TEF) for abusing its dominant position in the Spanish broadband markets will hold up in the European Court of First Instance if the Spanish telecommunication regulator decides to appeal the decision.

"The commission considers that its decision is legally sound. We have absolutely no reason to be afraid of a referral to the court of first instance," said commissions  antitrust spokesman Jonathan Todd.

TD
The commission's decision to  fine Telefonica  was very clearly referring to illegal action taken by Telefonica  which was harming Spanish consumers and businesses, Todd said. It wasn't aimed at the Spanish regulator, CMT, in any way, he added. The commission found in its ruling that the CMT had done its job properly.
CMT has requested the Spanish government to bring an annulment action before the court against the
EUR151.9 million  fine imposed on Telefonica.

The Spanish regulator accuses the commission of never formally having asked for the cooperation of the Spanish regulator, thus contravening European provisions.
The CMT said the commission decision "seriously and deeply affects" its regulatory competence. The European Commission opened a formal investigation into  Telefonica's  business practices in
February 2006. Telefonica  has said it will appeal the  fine.
Company Web sites:  www.cmt.es and www.telefonica.es

HD          Watchdog  declares war on Brussels over Telefónica fine for market abuse
BY          A. S.

SC          PAISE

CY          (c) 2007 EL PAIS, SL/IHT.

LP
The Spanish telecommunications supervisor on Thursday said that it had urged the government to appeal against a €152-million  fine imposed on Telefónica  by the European Commission for violating anti-trust rules.

The Telecommunications Market Commission (CMT) also lashed out at Brussels for invading its patch. The CMT had launched its own probe into allegations lodged by a competitor that Telefónica  had been overcharging rivals for access to its broadband ADSL internet network in order to stifle competition,
but absolved the Spanish telecoms giant of any wrongdoing.

TD
"The decision by the Commission seriously and profoundly affects the regulatory duties [of the CMT] in particular, and those of national regulatory agencies in general," the Spanish watchdog said in a statement. "This action compromises the achievement of [CMT's] objectives of regulating in defense of Spanish consumers," it added.

Telefónica  rejected Brussels' decision at the time as "unjustified and disproportionate," arguing that it had complied fully with CMT directives on pricing.

HD     El Pais: CMT asks Spanish government to lodge appeal against  Telefonica fine (La Comision de

LP
Following the European Commission's decision to impose a 152m-euro  fine on Spanish telecoms group Telefonica  for abuse of dominant position in the broadband internet market, the CMT, the Spanish telecommunications regulator, has asked the Spanish government to file an appeal against the  fine with the Luxemburg-based European Court of Justice. The CMT considers that the matter is the exclusive competence of the Spanish regulator and therefore outside the jurisdiction of Brussels.

TD
Appeals filed with the European Court of Justice against decisions made by Brussels can only be made by the company affected and the government of the member state in question. The Spanish government has so far only said that it will lodge an appeal if there is evidence of discrimination against  Telefonica  when compared with similar cases in other member states.  Telefonica  is being blamed for the fact that broadband access in Spain is 20 per cent more expensive and it reaches 20 per cent fewer people than
the European average. The Spanish government is looking carefully into the matter, as it does not want to defend Telefonica  at the expense of the users.

SE          Única
HD          Brussels digs heels in over Telefónica fine

BY          EL PAÍS WC         268 words PD          14 July 2007
SN          El Pais - English Edition
SC          PAISE
LA          English
CY          (c) 2007 EL PAIS, SL/IHT.

LP
The European Commission said Friday it was sticking by its decision to  fine Telefónica

€152 million for anti-trust activities despite a dispute with the Spanish telecommunications regulator over the move.

TD
The Telecommunications Market Commission (CMT) on Thursday urged the government to challenge the fine, which was imposed on Telefónica  for overcharging rivals for access to its broadband ADSL internet network in order to stifle competition. The penalty was the largest every imposed on a telecoms company by Brussels.
The CMT had launched its own probe into allegations of a so-called margin squeeze by  Telefónica
lodged by a competitor, but absolved the Spanish telecoms giant of any wrongdoing.

Speaking at a news conference yesterday in Brussels, Jonathan Todd, the spokesman for the Commission's competition department, said the European anti-trust authorities were convinced of the legal soundness of the decision to  fine Telefónica.

At the time the  fine was announced, Telefónica  said it would appeal against the Commission's "unjustified and disproportionate" ruling with the European Court of First Instance. The telecoms giant said it had fully complied with CMT directives on pricing and was caught between two regulators with conflicting opinions. Todd said the Commission had no problem with  Telefónica  appealing.

The CMT on Thursday also complained about interference by Brussels in its area of responsibility. It said the decision by the Commission "seriously and profoundly" affected the regulatory duties

of the CMT in particular and those of national regulators. It said it also undermined the CMT's duty of ensuring Spanish consumer were protected.

CR to ask EU to cover half of costs of fight against bird flu

Brussels - The Czech Republic will ask the  European Commission to cover 50 percent of costs of fight against bird flu that occurred in eastern Bohemia, Czech Agriculture Minister Petr Gandalovic told journalists here today.

TD
The Czech Republic could receive some Kc15m for the purpose, said Gandalovic, putting the overall costs at Kc25-30m.
CR almost alone in fight for sugar quotas redistribution

Brussels - The Czech Republic is almost alone in the fight for a different distribution of sugar quotas in the European Union, with its proposals being backed by Slovakia and Hungary only, Czech Agriculture Minister Petr Gandalovic told journalists in Brussels today.

Most other countries are for an overall cut of production by four-to-six million tonnes of sugar within the entire EU. Czechs want the EU to reflect previous adjustments of quotas in individual countries.
CzechRep against EU wine reform--minister

Brussels - The Czech Republic is among the majority of EU countries that are against the reform of the EU wine sector as presented recently by the  European Commission, Czech Agriculture Minister Petr Gandalovic told journalists at the meeting of EU farm ministers here today.

The proposal is supported by Spain and Italy only at the moment. Gandalovic said the reform probably has no chance to succeed.
Czech farmers harvest 14 pct of grains to date

Prague - Czech farmers have harvested 14 percent of 1.46 million hectares planted with grains this year, with average per hectare yield of 4.51 tonnes being eight percent higher against 2006, the Agriculture Ministry told CTK.

On the 338,000 hectares planted with rape, 43 percent has been harvested to date with average yield at three tonnes per hectare, the same as last year.
Car prices in CzechRep exceed European average

Prague - Prices of new cars in the Czech Republic for the first time exceeded European average at the end of the first quarter, as they were one percent above prices in eurozone countries, according to RoadtoData statistics published on the Internet.
Czech travel agencies report 10-pct rise in client numbers

Prague - Czech travel agencies have announced an extraordinarily successful season, as the number of their clients is roughly ten percent higher at the moment than it was a year ago, representatives of the travel agencies told CTK.

The share of supplementary goods on retailers' sales ranges between five and 20 percent and grows steadily.
Beer vending machine owners plan expansion in CR, abroad--CBW

Vending machines account for three-to-four percent of aggregate retail sales in the country, and their number has increased to an estimated 20,000 from 6,000-7,000 in the middle of the 1990s, said Cvejn.
EC calls for more detailed euro adoption steps in Slovakia

Brussels - Slovakia should focus within practical preparation for adoption of the single European currency especially on the securing of price stability after eurozone entry and prepare more detailed steps such as delivery of the new currency to banks and shops, the  European Commission said in a report today.
Slovakia wants to introduce the euro on January 1, 2009.

The Commission said that the Czech Republic is a good example of a country that has not set its eurozone entry date, but is carrying out early preparations.
PMU cuts fine for abuse of position by Slovak railway firm ZSR

help Telefonica  O2 in its fight for customers.

HD           European commission endorses  Nokia mobile TV technology
WC         681 words
PD          18 July 2007
SN          Guardian Unlimited
SC          GRULTD
LA           English
CY          Guardian Unlimited © Guardian Newspapers Limited 2007. All rights reserved

LP
Telecoms commissioner Viviane Reding courts the wrath of rivals by choosing Finnish company's
DVB-H as the common standard. By David Gow in Brussels

The European commission today courted the wrath of broadcasters and mobile phone operators by endorsing Nokia's DVB-H technology as the common standard for handheld television against other contenders.

TD
Viviane Reding, EU telecoms commissioner, stopped short of imposing Nokia's Digital Video Broadcasting for Handhelds but said she would include it in an official list of standards and look to mandating it in 2008. Operators and broadcasters would prefer Brussels to consider other technologies or allow each of the 27 EU states to adopt its own.

Ms Reding, who recently imposed binding "roaming" charges for overseas phone calls against a ferocious lobby by big mobile operators, insisted that a single standard technology would promote the uptake of mobile TV in time for next summer's Euro 2008 football tournament and the Beijing Olympics.

She wants a pan-European market and sees a strong risk of fragmentation through potentially 27 different sets of national rules, the uncoordinated use of spectrum and a lack of interoperability. She claims mobile TV could foster growth and jobs.

"Mobile broadcasting is a tremendous opportunity for Europe to maintain and expand its leadership in mobile technology and audiovisual services," she said. "Europe today is at a crossroads. We can either take the lead globally - as we did for mobile telephony based on the GSM standard developed by the European industry - or allow other regions to take the lion's share of the promising mobile TV market.

"Wait-and-see is not an option. The time has come for Europe's industry and governments to switch on to mobile TV."

Ms Reding argues that unless Europe takes concrete action immediately, it risks losing its competitive edge.

Penetration in Italy, the EU's most advanced market, is less than 1% compared with close to 10% in south Korea, Asia's most developed market. She estimates the market could be worth &#8364;20bn (£13.4bn) by 2011, reaching some 500 million customers globally.

The commission also urged governments to make radio spectrum - released by the switch from analogue to digital TV broadcasting - available for mobile TV as quickly as possible, including in the UHF band - and the so-called L-band as a backup. It called for "light touch" regulation of the nascent market.

The European Broadcasting Union said that the pace of technological development precluded the adoption of any one standard at this stage. It said it should be up to business to define attractive models that would entice consumers to opt for the standard they like best.

"Technology alone will not decide the future of mobile TV," said Fritz Pleitgen, EBU president and director-general of German public broadcaster WDR. "New devices will not be attractive unless they can show what the audience wants to see."


Page 143 of 186 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
The commission, meanwhile, threw an olive branch to mobile operators by dropping anti-trust proceedings against three big European groups - Vodafone, O2 and T-Mobile - after a six-year inquiry into "excessive" roaming tariffs that could have led to multimillion euro  fines of up to 10% of their relevant turnover.

It said the issue had been resolved by the new mandatory roaming charges (eurotariffs) which came into effect on July 1 and slashed current rates by up to 70%. Officials said it would have been a waste of taxpayers' money to continue the cases. "Whether or not those companies were guilty of  abuse has not been resolved but rather than take further time to reach a conclusion ... we consider it is not a worthwhile use of taxpayers' money."

Telefónica  O2 Europe welcomed the decision, reiterating that the case against it was "completely without foundation". Analysts said dropping the case cast doubt over the EU's anti-trust enforcement as it was unclear whether Brussels had been able to establish a case or not and whether consumers had been improperly charged hundreds of millions of euros in the past.
CO          nokia : Nokia Oyj

HD         FT.com site : Brussels closes antitrust case on 'roaming'. BY         Sarah Laitner in Brussels
WC        400 words
PD         19 July 2007
SN         Financial Times (FT.Com)
SC         FTCOM
LA         English
CY         (c) 2007 The Financial Times Limited. All rights reserved

LP
European Union  antitrust authorities closed on Wednesday long-running investigations into Vodafone and two other big mobile phone companies that allegedly charged excessive international call fees.

The decision to draw a line under the high-profile cases is unusual because EU competition regulators rarely stop such inquiries without either securing a settlement or imposing a fine.

TD
It comes amid heightened tensions between the  European Commission and mobile phone companies, many of which are enraged by a new EU law that forces them to cap lucrative international call tariffs.

The European Commission had in 2004 and 2005 issued formal charges against Vodafone UK and Germany, O2 UK and T-Mobile Germany, accusing them of abusing their dominant market position by demanding "unfair and excessive" roaming fees.

In particular, the regulator was concerned about the level of wholesale rates that they charged in the UK and Germany. These are fees that one operator pays another so that its customers can use the other's network.

However, the regulator said on Wednesday that the new law addressed the same issues as those raised in the antitrust proceedings and that it would close the cases as a result.

That controversial legislation, which surveys show is popular with consumers, was secured last month after a bruising fight between Brussels and the EU telecoms industry. The sector is estimated to make as much as 8.5bn ($11.7bn, GBP5.7bn) a year from roaming charges.

However, critics say that the law does not touch on pot-en-tial  competition infringe-ments, prompting speculation that the passage of the law provided a useful cover to drop investigations that had dragged for years.

A spokesman for Neelie Kroes, the EU  competition commissioner, said that with the law on roaming entering into force there was no longer any point in devoting time and resources to the  antitrust investigation.

The roaming legislation dealt with excessive charges in a very satisfactory manner, the spokesman added.

If the operators had been found guilty, they could have been  fined as much of 10 per cent of annual turn-over. However, it is rare for Brussels to impose the maximum penalty.

Telefonica  O2 Europe welcomed the decision to drop the allegations that O2 UK had breached
competition law. The company said that the case against it was completely without foundation.

HD     Expansion: Telefonica  to pay fine (Telefonica  opta por pagar la multa de Kroes en vez de avalarla). WC    194 words
PD     21 July 2007
SN     Expansión SC     EXPNAB LA      English
CY     The Financial Times Limited. European Intelligence Wire. All material subject to copyright. Expansion ©
2007 All rights reserved.

LP
Telefonica,  the Spanish telecommunications group, has decided to pay a  fine of 151.87m euros it was ordered to pay by the  European Commission earlier this month. While it could have opted to present a bank guarantee for this amount, it has decided not to and will pay the  fine. However, the decision to pay does not alter  Telefonica's  absolute rejection of the  fine; it is currently preparing its appeal to have the penalty declared null and void before the European Court of Justice in Luxembourg. The appeal must be submitted by September 20.

This fine, the largest ever imposed by the European Commission on a telco, was imposed on the Spanish operator after the regulator ruled that Telefonica  had hindered competition in the Spanish ADSL market. Even so, the  fine will have a limited impact on Telefonica's  bottom line: in the three months to March 31, it recorded a net profit of 1.257bn euros, up 7.7 per cent on a year earlier.

TD

GERVAIS PELLISSIER: I think the execution of the transformation costs you mentioned, you're right, in France for the first half 2006 you mentioned [it at 85]. It's [EUR100m] of costs. We do not mention it this year because it's true that it was as I mentioned at the beginning of my speech, we're clearly in the ongoing process of transformation this year. I think now part of those costs are part of the structure, especially all
the costs to support the new offers are now embedded in the structure. And on some of the others we have worked to get them down. This explains some of the improvements we have. I'm not sure it's worthwhile to continue to focus on that, but it's rather I think they are now beyond this stage of transformation. Even if there's still a lot to go on the [home] part of the business.
THIERRY BAUDIN: So you would consider they are down to a fraction of what they were a year ago? GERVAIS PELLISSIER: Yes.
THIERRY BAUDIN: Okay. And the bulk of the staff cuts impact of EUR85m quarter on quarter and the
IT&N savings that were highlighted, you would argue that to a large extent they would be allocated to home
France along with the new pricing arrangements with the enterprise segment?

GERVAIS PELLISSIER: I'm not sure I am completely -- no, I'm not sure that's completely right. But -- because if you transform the infrastructure, you see a evolution enterprise compared to the evolution on
the French home margin. You see that the proportion of businesses are very different. So the weight in the margin are different. What's important for the enterprise division is less important in terms of impact for the home France division because of the respective sizes of the business. So you cannot make a comparison one for one. So that's one point.

The second point is that I think this change of prices has already reached really for (inaudible) of the debate. It is also linked with the trends in the business. We have to change the base and there are a lot of internal debates whether these are the right prices, but it's also a reflection of some of the prices evolution of some the other parties.

UNIDENTIFIED COMPANY REPRESENTATIVE: Thank you. And thank you all for having participated to this call. I'm really pleased with my colleagues, especially Vincent and the Investor Relations team, to meet most of you maybe just after a few vacations. So for those who are leaving, I wish you a good vacation and I hope that these results we have provide to you has allowed you to have a good vacation. Thank you.

OVERVIEW
Management reported that 1H07 revenue was EUR25.9b, growth of 1.9%. 1H07 net income was EUR3.3b. FINANCIAL DATA
A. Key Data From Call 1. 1H07 revenue = EUR25.9b. 2. 1H07 net income = EUR3.3b. PRESENTATION SUMMARY
S1. Financial Review (G.P.) 1. Highlights: 1. FTE has been able to achieve what it wanted to achieve. 1. Stabilization of profitability and gross operating margin (GOM). 2. A better revenue situation than last year, especially in 2Q, with a 2% revenue growth vs. a year ago. 2. On track to reach 2007 guidance regarding profitability and CapEx. 1. FTE is able to commit on a stable organic cash flow for the period 2006-2008, as it was slightly up early in 2006. 3. Has developed enough action to sustain performance in 2007 and to lay already some foundation for 2007. 4. Continuing to re-engineer its processes within the group in order to enhance the level of service and to reduce cost structure. 2. 1H07 Financial Achievements: 1. 1.9%
revenue growth to EUR25.9b. 1. This comes from a strong performance in domestic, fixed, and mobile operations for France. 2. Some recovery in other European markets. 3. A much better performance for enterprise than a year ago. 4. Sustained performance of fast-growing markets, which continued to contribute strongly to growth. 2. GOM stabilization comes mainly from France, where there is recovery in
the profitability and the continued contribution of fast-growing markets, where GOM continued to increase in line with increase in revenue. 3. Level of spending in CapEx is slightly below 2006 at the end of 1H. 1. On the basis of the programs, which are underway in terms of large investments within the group, FTE
confirms full-year objective of 13% to revenue. 4. Has an organic cash flow, which has slightly increased over 1H06. 1. Confirms the full-year objective of EUR6.8b. 5. Organic cash flow in 1H07 is mainly dedicated to the payment of the 2006 dividend. 1. Level of debt remains stable vs. the beginning of the year. 2. In 2H, cash flow is used for the debt investment. 3. 1H07 Operational Achievements: 1. Total customer base is
163m customers, out of which 102.5m mobile customers, an increase of 15%. 2. With the mobile customer base, 9m mobile customers are broadband mobile customers, which is multiplication by three for the course of the last 12 months. 3. Fixed broadband business, DSL, FTE has now 10.5m subscribers. 1. Remains the leader on the European market. 2. 50% of the customer base is equipped with Livebox. 3. 35% of the customers are using VoIP. 4. 8% are using IPTV. 5. FTE is now 12% of DSL customer base using TV over IP. 4. Enterprise: 1. On top of the global revenue performance, there is a continued development of the convergence of services, especially Business Everywhere in France, with 525,000 customers plus 20% vs.
a year ago. 2. IP/VPN accesses with 273,000, 20% on top of last year. 3. Strong performance in services

Page 171 of 186 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
revenue, which is increasing by 16%. 4. NExT Strategy: 1. Stated two years ago in June 2005, when FTE launched the NExT strategy, that a huge part of the future growth would come on value-added services on top of access and from convergence services. 2. Path coming from value-added services, including Internet access plus content plus all the value-added services on top of access is now representing 22% of the revenue in the mature countries. 1. It was representing only 18% of the revenues in mature markets, mainly Western Europe markets, three years ago. 3. Traditional PSTN and voice access, which was representing
38% of revenue in 2005 is now representing 29%. 1. A drop by 10 points of the contribution of legacy voice and access business to the revenue. 4. Mobile has increased and is stable, a little below 50% from the
total. 1. The fact that FTE was right to push of this technology move and technology evolution of the customer base, because this is one way to compete successfully in the future, and to maintain market share with new businesses. 2. This is the explanation of content pressure FTE has had on the margin, and
the need to adjust skills, tools with this cost structure with this new technology. 5. Fast-Growing Markets: 1. Strong evolution in the global revenue picture. 2. They are now accounting for 13% of global revenue, whereas it is representing 10% two years ago. 6. Profitability: 1. FTE is coming back to the stabilization at the level it had a year ago. 2. GOM before commercial expense has even slightly improved more,
especially in 2Q07 than GOM after commercial expense. 3. Good margin evolution is mainly coming from the improvement of the cost structure on top of the revenue dynamics. 4. Labor costs have been decreasing by 0.4% of revenue in one year. 5. Interconnection costs have been much better managed in
2007. 1. FTE had started to improve the situation at the end of 2006. 2. Had a deterioration of interconnect expense in percentage point of revenue in 2005 and 1H06. 3. Has growth on the mobile and the fixed business to improve the cost structure of the business, especially with massive introduction of unlimited and abundance offers on its base, and to come down now to 4. 15% to revenue. 6. Other IT and network costs remained flat. 7. Commercial expenses have slightly increased. 8. General, properties and others: 1. Increase was mainly linked with some accruals, moves and reversals of accruals on some risk, especially a reversal of Lebanon in 2006 and some further accruals in 2007. 7. Headcount: 1. Has been able to reduce the headcount by a little less than 8,000 people in one year since June 2006. 1. Out of which 1,571 net departures has been realized in 1H07 in France, implying that 60% of three-year plan is now achieved at
the end of June 2007. 2. FTE is confident that it will achieve the three-year plan, which accounts for 17,000 net departures between 2006-2008. 8. Interconnect, IT & Networks Costs: 1. When measuring them as a whole, including labor costs, FTE has improved them by EUR140m vs. a year ago, a decrease of more
than 2% vs. last year. 1. This is linked with better management of the gap between what FTE pays to other operators and so to take the full benefit of the termination rate cuts when they are there. 2. Not to pay more in other situations, and got to increase revenue or not to decrease the revenue. 2. Has some slight increase of the non-labor IT and network costs, which is linked with the deployment of the customer service platform and the ongoing roll out of networks. 1. Partially offset by the outsourcing of some of the dealers, especially in Belgium and Netherlands. 3. Counts on further savings potential with the networking agreement that FTE starts to be working in Spain in 2H07 and in 2008. 9. Operating Income & Net Income: 1. Has increased operating income by EUR324m at EUR5.5b. 1. Half of the improvement is increase to GOM improvement.
2. There is an increase of the capital gains on the assets disposals, with the sale of the remaining stake in TDF and Eutelsat. 3. Partly offset by some increase of the depreciation on fixed assets, also an increase in mobile investments in Spain and in fast-growing countries. 2. Net income at Group level at EUR3.3b, benefiting from a strong reduction in the tax P&L linked with the increase of deferred tax assets in France by little less than EUR600m, and the decrease of the UK tax rate from 30% to 28%, which brings an additional EUR80m proceeds in the P&L. 1. There is a reduction of net income part of the minority shareholders and increased sale of Yellow Pages, which is no longer in FTE's account. 2. Excluding the
exceptional items, FTE has increased net income by EUR180m vs. last year to come to EUR2.4b. 10. Cash Flow & Debt: 1. Increase of cash flow is mainly linked with the increase of GOM, to be at EUR3.3b vs. EUR3.1b a year ago. 1. This improvement makes FTE comfortable to achieve thee total year objective. 2. There is no change regarding the debt, as the totality of the cash flow has been dedicated to the dividend payment. 1. There are few other movements between proceeds of sales of assets and some small acquisitions. 11. 1H07 France: 1. Has good performance on the personal division, on the mobile business with a stable revenue, slightly above a year ago. 2. A small recovery in 2Q07 vs. the situation at the end of [3Q06] where FTE is slightly declining. 3. 40.2% GOM rate to revenue vs. 39.5% a year ago. 4. Has been able to stabilize market share in retail and to come back to a good level of market share, including MVNOs at the end of 1H07. 1. There has been a continuous strategic fit with more pay monthly customers, which now represent more than 64% of the customer base. 2. Strong dynamics in terms of broadband mobile,
with a multiplication by about three of the customer base, which is now a little more than 20% of the total customer base. 5. Internet plus Fixed: 1. Has now been able to fully offset the decline of traditional PSTN by the increase in Internet and multi-play revenues. 2. GOM has increased from 32.4% to 35.4% in one year. 1. There is still an increase of the total number of telecom lines on the French market. 2. There are now 27,840 lines, which is about 100,000 more than at the end of 2006. 3. On the DSL market, FTE has
been able to keep its market share at 49.2% installed base, due to good dynamics in acquisitions, because market share of net adds has come back to deliver a 47.8% in 2Q07. 6. Broadband ARPU: 1. Standing at a little more than EUR30 at the end of 2Q07, an increase of 11% vs. a year ago. 1. Due to the deployment of more multi-play offers on customer base. 7. New vs. year ago: 1. Strong development of VOD accesses, with 900,000 paid VOD accesses in 1H07, which is a multiplication by five vs. a year ago and a
Page 172 of 186 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
multiplication by two vs. 2H06. 2. Has now launched new offers this year regarding VoIP to continue the deployment of VoIP, which is now sold on 46% of customer base in France vs. 28% a year ago. 8. UNIK: 1. There has been a strong increase vs. the situation at the end of 2006, with now 300,000 UNIK terminals sold on customer base. 1. Increasing of the full range of models for 2H07, which makes the product not
only for specific customers or specific situations, but allows to increase the potential on the market. 2. Has opened UNIK on the 30,000 Orange Wi-Fi hot spots in France. 1. Plus facility to connect UNIK phones on the Livebox of other Orange DSL users, which makes the UNIK phone a real VoIP and mobile phone depending on the location on the French territory. 9. Fiber: 1. Fiber development is on track with the plan announced at the end of 2006. 2. Has a little more than 2,000 customers who have signed a fiber contract, which is two times what FTE had at the end of last year. 3. 27,000 potential customers, 27,000 flats where fiber is now available because agreements have been made with the building managers of 27,000 flats. 10. Has spent EUR10m in CapEx until the end of June. 11. FTE is either in the course of installing or about to install fiber in ten cities outside of Paris. 12. Priorities & Action Plan: 1. Focus on mobile is to maintain the market share in a situation where there is additional pressure with the number portability, which FTE takes full effect in 2H07. 2. Taking into account the roaming regulation, which is impacting revenues and GOM in this year. 13. Home Division: 1. FTE has to continue to push for better customer satisfaction. 1. Ahead of competitors, but needs to be even better. 2. Has to target more and more precisely customer base to adapt the offer to the needs of customer, especially between naked DSL. 3. Traditional PSTN subscription is to try to focus on the (indiscernible), where naked DSL is a strong tool to recover market share. 12. UK: 1. Has good organic growth, with 3.1% growth in 1H07 on the mobile business. 1. This is an improved quality of subscriber base. 2. In the very competitive situation of the UK market, FTE has decided to focus on the
high-value customers, especially to remain the leader within the customer segment, where customers pay more than GBP35 a month. 3. An increased proportion of data and value-added tariff revenue on the customer base linked with the development of 3G. 4. Mobile Operations: 1. They are seeing a good recovery in 2Q07. 2. Strong net adds in terms of contract days. 3. Strong increase of the customer base in terms of pay monthly customers, a 10% increase at the end of 1H07 vs. end of 1H06. 4. Good level of ARPU. 5. Direct distribution represented 41% of the net adds on 1H07 vs. 30% a year ago. 6. Broadband:
1. Situations remain highly challenging, with revenue down by 4%. 1. This is mainly linked with the decline of narrowband whereas this remains difficult to continue to deploy the unbundling, and to acquire
customers in DSL in the UK. 2. Has grown DSL customer base by 9% in one year. 3. Tries to keep a stable ARPU in a very competitive environment, where most of the new entrants are presenting DSL access or Internet connections as add-ons on something like pay-TV subscriptions or voice subscriptions or anything else. 4. Continues to focus on quality of service. 5. In spite of a regulatory environment, real situation in terms of unbundling remains not so easy. 7. Action Plans: 1. Has to increase and to recover in prepaid markets, but also keeping the high-value strategy on the prepaid market, not deteriorating the value. 2. Has to pursue the development of loyalty within the customer base and to continue to work strongly on the cost structure, including the infrastructure and network costs with the implementation of network-sharing agreements with Vodafone to prepare for acquisitions in 2008. 8. Internet: 1. One of the weaknesses in
1H07, FTE needed to raise brand awareness in terms of Internet access. 2. Orange is a strong mobile brand. 3. Has to take the opportunity of the launch of more aspects in dual play and to start with some triple play, including TV offers at the end of the year to conquer again some market share. 13. Spain: 1. Situation in mobile has been better than expected, especially with some increase in revenue and some recovery on GOM in 2Q07 vs. 1Q07. 2. Had few negative effects on the revenue, mainly linked with some difficulties
with some unlimited offers, which have created trouble at the margin and revenue level. 1. This is recovering in 2Q07. 3. Has strong net adds in 1Q07 and even more in 2Q07. 1. Has been obliged to take into account the loss of Euskaltel DSL customers. 2. Has decided to clean the prepaid customer base, where there were lots of inactive customers. 3. Has a stable customer base vs. a year ago. 4. Has stable ARPU vs. a year ago. 4. Internet & Fixed: 1. Has good growth in terms of customer base, 18% increase of the customer base. 2. Strongly focused acquisitions and strongly focused on unbundled areas. 3. FTE is now at 60% growth of the customer base in unbundled areas. 4. Declining the number of customers, which are not in the unbundled areas. 1. This has not been enough to offset in terms of revenue. 2. Strong decline of voice and narrowband, does not have enough revenue increase on the Internet to offset the decline in voice and narrowband. 5. Integration with Ya.com, Ya.com has been finally acquired on 07/31/07. 5. Action Plan: 1. A new CEO has come on board at the end of June in Spain. 2. FTE is going to keep the
momentum in customer acquisition in mobile, especially in contract. 3. Has to continue and to finalize the coverage in terms of 3G, including doing it through networking agreement with Vodafone. 4. Has to
continue its fight to limit the churn. 1. Has decreased churn rate vs. a year ago. 5. To launch the MVNOs: 1. Some MVNOs contract has been signed in the course of last year. 2. There is a potential to grow customer base for MVNOs. 6. Home Market: 1. Needs to continue to reinforce DSL market share. 2. With Ya.com, FTE is clearly the number one alternative to the incumbent, and needs to push that in the course of 2H07.
14. Poland: 1. Good success in mobile. 1. They have continued to increase their market share in mobile and to maintain a strong profitability with 38.5% GOM rate. 2. FTE has continued to grow the customer base, especially for broadband, and it will continue to do that. 3. Action Plan: 1. Action plan for 2H07 is on mobile to continue to remain ahead in terms of market share, to continue to grow market share, to pursue the stimulation of the 3G usage, and specific customer growth. 2. Regarding broadband, FTE has put in place a new offer that should be operational in Sept. 15. Other Countries: 1. Growth comes from either
Page 173 of 186 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Eastern Europe, Middle East, Africa, and Caribbean, where most of those countries are growing above
20%, a little less in Eastern Europe, 17%. 2. With continued growth of the consumer base, more than 50%
growth in Middle East, Africa, Caribbean whereas customer base growth remained at 17% in Eastern
Europe. 1. This has helped to provide Group with additional profit as the total GOM rate for both countries,
including the Western Europe countries, is at 41.8% vs. 42% a year ago. 3. Home Market: 1. A huge part of
the customer base was represented by Orange Netherlands, which is on sale. 2. Looking at the broadband
situation, FTE has now not far from 100,000 customers in Ivory Coast, Senegal, Mauritius, and Jordan,
which is the beginning of the broadband Internet business in those countries. 3. Believes this is an area of
development for the future, on top of the dynamics within mobile. 4. Action plan is mainly to keep the
growth momentum and to start to develop alternative networks, including WiMAX or FTTH in some of the
countries. 16. Enterprise: 1. Revenue has been much better than a year ago, with a strong improving trend,
especially looking at the situation in 2Q07 where revenue decline has been nearly to 0.4% of revenue,
where it was [nearly 2%] decline in 1Q07. 1. This is linked with the clear decline of some of the legacy
business, especially the voice legacy revenue in France and outside of France. 2. In terms of advanced
business network, FTE has a continuous increase of the IP revenue, even it is at a slower pace than it was
a year ago, which helped to maintain the legacy revenues and in spite of strong pressure for international
prices. 3. ICT services have continued to grow at a higher rate of the market 15.5%, and they now
represent 24% of the revenues of the division. 4. Profitability: 1. There has been a decline of 2.5 points,
because it was last year when FTE restated it to compare it to 2007, it was at 19.5%. 1. This is below the
figure that was published last year. 2. Has reassessed its internal transfer price between enterprise and the
home France division. 2. In spite of that at 17% to revenue, FTE remains clearly above major competitors
who are trying to act in terms of [high yield], especially the British one and the German one. 5. Action plan
for enterprise is to continue to secure the legacy business, to pursue the enhancement of portfolio on VoIP,
and to continue to streamline the cost base. 17. Outlook: 1. FTE does not expect in 2H07 a big difference
vs. 1H07 in terms of revenue evolution. 2. In terms of profit, situation is slightly different, because FTE
knows that there will be a little more regulatory pressure. 1. Roaming will have an impact on GOM in
France. 3. Has the profitability number effects in France, which could create some pressure on the profit,
including the need to increase some of the subsidies to keep the customers. 4. Has clearly the difficulties of
the regulatory environment in Poland. 5. Knows that in some countries like the UK or Spain, competitive
environment will remain tough, because the incumbent remains highly protected by the local regulatory
authorities or because the nature of the market that there are too many players likely to be placed. 1.
Before consolidation happens, there is still huge  competition. 6. Confirms guidance for 2H07 in terms of
margin, in terms of cash flow. 7. Will continue to work on business portfolio finalizing some of the decisions,
which have been made like the sale of Orange Netherlands, and to continue to buy [certain] of the
businesses. 8. Confirmed Guidance: 1. Near stabilization of GOM. 2. To maintain CapEx rate at the level of
13%. 3. To maintain organic cash flow at EUR6.8b in 2007, but also in 2008, including some investments,
that could impact directly the cash flow like acquisition of the 3G license in Egypt.
QUESTION AND ANSWER SUMMARY

DAMIEN MALTARP, ANALYST, CAZENOVE: Thanks. It's Damien Maltarp here from Cazenove. I've got two questions. The first one, I was just wondering if you could comment on Iliad's application for the fourth
3G license. Do you see them as very much a credible competitor to your mobile business?

And secondly, any thoughts on their proposal to defer the payment of the license fee would be of interest. And do you think that is something you could potentially replicate as well?

And the second question is just going back to the changes to the mobile number portability. It's been a couple of months now since that was introduced into France. Can you just give us an indication of what your -- what you've seen so far, and therefore what are the implications for costs going forward? Thanks.

VINCENT BENOIT, IR, FRANCE TELECOM: Well, sorry, we didn't hear you very well. Can you summarize quickly your first and second questions, please?
DAMIEN MALTARP: Yes. Can you hear me now? VINCENT BENOIT: (Multiple speakers) top of your mike. DAMIEN MALTARP: Can you hear me now?
GERVAIS PELLISSIER, CFO, FRANCE TELECOM: A bit better, but if you can speak louder it would be nice.

DAMIEN MALTARP: Okay. I will try now. The first question was on Iliad's 3G license application, just your thoughts on whether you see them as a credible competitor to you on the mobile side, and also any thoughts on their proposal for the deferred payment of the license fee.


Page 174 of 186 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
And also, just the second one was on mobile number portability. We are a couple of months in. Just what you are seeing, the initial view on what has changed since it was introduced.

GERVAIS PELLISSIER: I will hand over the question to Benoit. So, the first question is on the -- what do we think of the Iliad position in terms of 3G license. And the second question is on the effects, how do we see the effects of the number portability up to now.

BENOIT EYMARD, FRANCE SALES AND SERVICES, FRANCE TELECOM: So, regarding Iliad, as you have noticed it, as they are the only one who have been candidates, but the proposal they have made so far in their press release do not fit into the conditions that have been established by the French regulator. So it's up to now the reg authorities to make their comments on the Iliad proposal. And if they consider that
it does not fit into the conditions that were set, they will have to consider that the bid for the license will have to be reopened, which would open a new period of four to six months of new process for the fourth license
in France.

I don't think it's in our position to make much more comment on Iliad's credibility, to take your question regarding the deployment of a fourth network in France. We just all know that it will take a lot of time and that, as you know, the French market is a difficult one for minor operators since France is the biggest country in Europe with more than 500,000 square kilometers. It is, therefore, the most expensive to cover, as we all know. Just to give a comparison, between our French operations and English operation, the cost is almost 30% more to cover to provide an accurate 3G network. This is one comment.

The second comment to be made is that, as you know, there are growing environmental pressures for any new network to be deployed, and this is clearly one of the stakes behind the subject of the fourth 3G license in France.

Regarding number portability, we think that the need is to be very cautious since, as Gervais stated it, it's only two months now that the number portability new condition has been put into place. Just as a reminder, number portability has been in France already three years but it was under a two-stop shopping process, and we have now -- we are now operating under a one-stop shopping process.

So far, we must also acknowledge that the first few years are better than what we could expect in terms of equilibrium regarding the Orange base of the effects of number portability, especially for the business market and for the value customers with subscription more than two hours, in which we have gained more than we have been losing to our competitors for number portability.

So, therefore, up to now we consider that the news are quite good. But once again, we remain very cautious because we consider that the key changes we should see on the French market will occur during Q3 and Q4 on the French market.
DAMIEN MALTARP: Okay. Thanks a lot.

NICK LYLE, ANALYST, UBS: Hi. It's Nick Lyle from UBS. Could I ask three quick questions? Just the first one, could you explain the benefit from the lack of sale -- or rather the benefit from the lack of rebranding in the Q2 numbers, just to give us a rough idea of what's lack of rebranding and what's genuine savings?
